This is a hidden gem in Westbrook village. The hotel is absolutely gorgeous, clean and located in the quiet area of LA, between Santa Monica and Beverly hills. The staff is incredible, we upgraded our room the same day, everyone from front desk to housekeeping was very friendly. They have a really nice rooftop with tables and seating area. They have a garage conveniently located. We will be coming back!</Review>

<UserId.>107686902010944202580< /UserId.><username>Dontae Delgado</username><date>1547754902029< /date><Rate>5</Rate>< Text>
Absolutely fantastic place to stay. A hidden gem that is still building out it's property, so the best of yet to come.

Customer service: top notch. They know your name from the moment you walk in. Front the room service to the director, they respect and treat you like royalty.

Rooms: very clean. The European architecture is a welcome change from the typical modern-looking hotels. Very roomy, full kitchen, washer & dryer, and a fantastic bed.

Amenities: They are building up a restaurant, Continental breakfast, and more! They have a rooftop area with fresh fruit that you can pick! It was raining on our visit (but that didn't prevent us from enjoying it!), but this would be amazing during a sunny day.

I will absolutely stay here again and look forward to they growth as a company. A membership setup would be ideal.<//Text>

<GmapID>0x80c2bc81c95c48f9:0x8341e978a4695b28< /GmapID>< text>
This is probably one of the nicest hotels at which we have ever stayed.  We had an early-morning appointment about 1/2 a mile away and I thought it would be nice to splurge a little and not have to deal with Los Angeles freeway traffic early in the morning. So, we drove to L.A. the night before and stayed here.The hotel itself was amazing.  Check-in was a breeze and all of the staff were friendly and welcoming.  The hotel has its own parking structure with roll-up gates, so the car was quite secure.  I think they have the fastest elevator I have ever ridden.  We reserved the Premier Suite (wow).  It was like a small condo, with a dining area, a living room, and a kitchenette.  It is definitely set up for long-term guests.  There were two balconies; one overlooking the city street and restaurant scene with a view of the mountains to the northeast.  From the wood floors to the huge walk-in shower and walk-in closet, this place was amazing.  There was a Kurig coffee maker with an assortment of coffee, tea, and hot chocolate. The bed was very comfortable.  There was a huge flat screen TV with a full DirecTV lineup.  The room was quiet and the climate control worked well without keeping us up at night.There are lots of restaurants withing walking distance.  Shopping was pretty much closed down due to the over-hyped virus, but that wasn't the fault of the hotel.If you're going to Westwood, stay here!</text>

<UserId.>109981776128652220786< /UserId.><Name>Emilee Unterkoefler< /Name><time>1609175447595</time><Rate>5< /Rate>< text>
Plaza La Reina is both a luxurious getaway and a most comforting stay when you are away from home. The staff is what has drawn us back time and again, as they are all accomodating, friendly, attentive to our needs. The folks (shout out to Troy, Taylor, and Philippe, and AJ) always went above and beyond in ensuring that we had everything we needed for a comfortable stay and consistently did so with genuine smiles. The hotel is immaculately clean, and we felt comfortable letting our toddler crawl in the room (which we've never done in other hotels). The room's kitchenette and washing machine/drier were convenient for us. The prime location is close to many local restaurants and other necessary places like Ralphs (grocery store) and Target. During a difficult time in our lives, the staff and our stay as a whole helped our family tremendously, and we'd recommend this location to anyone visiting Westwood.<//text>

< Text>
I stayed there once previously and mentioned that it would be very helpful to business people if the hotel could provide the means to scan and email documents. At my most recent stay, several months later, they had added this capacity. That is just one example of their desire to accommodate customers needs. Beautiful large, clean, modern rooms, complete with small ‚ÄúKitchen ‚Äú area with coffee/tea maker, sink , dishes and glassware, refrigerator and dishwasher. For the quality of the rooms and hotel generally and  great Westwood location, by LA standards it is not expensive. As our daughter, her husband and newborn live in Westwood, we expect to be visiting from our home in Florida , every two to three months and will not stay anywhere else. We have travelled extensively both in the U.S. and internationally and this is one of the finest hotels we have experienced. You will not be disappointed.< /Text>

< Text>
Stayed here for one night on Oct. 9 for a business trip to UCLA, to which the hotel is very close.  The best way to describe my stay was as if I was visiting a boutique hotel in Europe.  The front desk and manager called me by name from the time I arrived, and were very available to give information about the room/hotel and the area.  The room was beautiful.  It included a kitchen set up, pretty much everything you'd need if you were there for an extended stay.  The bed was extremely comfortable, and the bathroom was immaculate, beautiful and very functional.  I highly recommend Plaza La Reina.  The way that the building looks from the outside does not do the inside justice, but once inside I experienced one of the best hotel stays in recent memory.</Text>

< Text>
A few years ago this place was amazing. Sushi was fantastic, the service was great, and they brought you you sushi in a timely manner. Now, however,  that has been totally turned around. The all you can eat sushi has become more expensive for less quality. Some servers piratically throw your glass of water on the table when you arrive and then never re-fill it for the remainder of the time your there. But the part that really gets me is the wait time on all you can eat Sushi. The past 5 or so times we've been there, one plate of sushi takes 40+ minutes to make. They also lose your order sometimes, and then when you ask the server why, they begin pointing figures at their co-workers (I even had the manager start pointing fingers at his own employees. Can't be the manager's fault, right?). Last time I was there, their excuse was "We don't have that product in stalk at the moment." which is perfectly fine. I understand. What I don't understand is why it took you 40 minutes to tell us that, and now we have to re-order and wait another 40 minutes. I don't want to sit here for 3 hours for only 3 plates of sushi. Sorry, but I will never go back.< /Text>

I am giving 4 stars because I love sushi, and this place delivers! Granted, we have been here many many times in the past, and the service is up and down? What's up with that?
Look, I've read a lot of reviews from others, and can see why communication can seem confusing at best. That said, I have seen a glimmer of hope with renewed staff, buy it appears that the bottom line is thier only concern. Maybe I'm wrong, and please stop me if I am, but the turn around here is like a roller coaster?
Maybe a little off track,but I am trying to address many pro's and con's.
For a while, my family and I went trekking for other sushi places in and out of the area, but as it stands, we ended up right back here....
Maybe I am a little more patient than others, and with that I look for an attempt by the servers trying to get it right. The ones that don't, get what's owed to them.
Look, it's not that difficult. Approach your customers with respect, and a smile. Drop by every few minutes, and you'd be surprised at how people (customers) react.
In closing, I would like the owners, or managerial staff to read these reviews every once in a while, that way when we return, and the service has pleased us, well - you get the idea.< /Review>

<text>The waiters and waitress' are great, but the way things work at the restaurant is atrociously sad. I have only eaten their sushi and so I know nothing about the hibachi/steakhouse. It's "all you can eat" or "eat all you can" sushi based on what they say, but to me it is ALL YOU CAN EAT RICE. If I wanted to eat rice as the majority of my meal I would have gone home to eat and pay a fraction of my bill. I don't recommend sitting at the bar because their tempura chips have spilled on my food before. The chefs take their time making their sushi and seem like young inexperienced chefs due to how all the fish is pre-cut. My girlfriend and I ate our order in less than ten minutes and the quality of the fish was as if it was purchased at Costco. We waited nearly an hour for just some sashimi and 2 rolls. They try to serve everything all at once so it makes you get full much faster than usual because the more there is to see the lower your appetite. The girl next to us got their order before we did and she came in ten minutes later after we got seated. I have had a better experience at both inexpensive and expensive sushi restaurants and this in my opinion was the "third time's the charm" experience. Third time I went there and the last time I will go there. DON'T ORDER THE NIGIRI because the amount of rice they put is size of three gumballs. Right  before big B-day gathering our Amana bottom freezer refrigerator was over freezing everything in there. We just did our grocery's for over $200 , fresh organic veggies and fruits won't last long , couldn't imagine the worst case scenario than that.
First we called to our  repairman whom we used for years but , he wasn't around and we start calling to local companies , the fastest service we have been offered  was by  Repairbest , they sent tech  named Vadim out the same day.
After diagnosing it  , and find out that  thermostat needs to be replaced. He checked the stock  and told us that he will be back in 3 hours and guess what , he was back on time  and replaced the part and left us with perfectly working fridge.
Couldn't be happier .
Thank you Vadim and Repairbest!
Will definitely call again.</Text>

<Review>Spectrum is the new kid on the block in terms of cell phones and moving to them was nothing short of a nightmare.

First, it is important to know that Spectrum is now allowing customers to ‚ÄúBYOD‚Äù ‚Äì bring your own device. However, they only allow certain iPhones on the BYOD plan. Since my iPhone 7Plus was tethered to the carrier, I knew my device would be exempted and I would need to either buy a device from Spectrum or purchase from the Apple Store. So, I stopped into the local Spectrum in Hemet to ask some questions. I quickly found out that Hemet Spectrum is not yet equipped to provide cell service and are referring customers to the Moreno Valley location. They did provide what information they were able and even called the Moreno Valley store to ensure they could answer some basic questions. They did confirm that any of the new iPhones could be brought over to Spectrum.

I drove 45-min to the closest Apple Store (Temecula) to purchase the new iPhone XR. That excursion took about 5 hours between the purchase, transfer of data, and drive. This does not include the hours spent since iCloud did not transfer over any of my app username or passwords (I‚Äôll save that for Apple‚Äôs review).

It took me about a week to make it to the Moreno Valley Spectrum (a 45-min drive) to get the phone connected, a regretful delay. When I showed up on Monday morning, I was told that over the weekend, Spectrum was no longer able to provide service for iPhone XR, XS or XS Max. What!? I returned home disappointed and perturbed.

I had to return the phone to Temecula and the Apple store was gracious in allowing the return. I tried to google a phone number to make a simple call to Spectrum in Moreno Valley, simply to determine if they had the iPhone XR 128G in stock as I was now without my iPhone. Apparently, the store does not accept customer calls and no one at the main Spectrum number knew how to reach them. Customer Service wanted me to order the phone and have it shipped, which was not what I was wanting.

Next day, I returned to Moreno Valley Spectrum to see if they had any phones in stock. Turns out they did, but not the color I wanted ‚Äì but hey, I had already spent so much time driving back and forth, I wasn‚Äôt going to let color stand between me and my new phone. Black it is.

From there, it was a breeze. The new phone was set up easily and quickly. The phone purchase and even the startup of my son‚Äôs iPhone X (BYOD) was no hassle at all.

Now for the reason Spectrum received 3 stars after all the hassle of changing my phone and about 10 hours of hassle (drive time, purchasing/returning phones, research/investigation, etc.). Christian was great and knew his stuff when transferring over the phones but the real star is Norvella S.

Norvella is amazing! She is the one who made this whole process bearable. I may have given up transferring my phone to Spectrum had it not been for her (& some cost savings from Verizon). The first time I showed up to Moreno Valley Spectrum, Norella was the one who assisted me. She was kind, friendly, smiled, made eye contact, laughed and made a connection with me as a customer. She apologized for the inconvenience and gave me a card with her name, promising that if I returned, I could present the card and skip the line.

When I returned to the store today, Norvella was helping another person but when she looked up, she immediately recognized me and smiled. She allowed me to skip the long line and got right down to business. Norvella is the ultimate customer service representative that any business would want. Because I am a manager myself, I stopped on my way out to ask for her manager to tell him what a great employee he has in Norvella.

Incidentally, the manager told me that he is opening a store in Menifee (yay! ‚Äì closer to Hemet) and that Norvella will be working there. So, if you move your cell phone to Spectrum, look for Norvella at the Menifee store starting May 2019.</Review>< time>

<Rating>3<//Rating><Text>As of July 2017, this is a pretty new Motel 6; at least, the interior is new.

It was nice not to have ash trays in the room, finally! There was a very slight tobacco odor, though. It was not bad, but there were two cigarette burns on the tub. Some people just don't obey the rules!

Many of the bright-white towels had some type of mark on them. I suppose it is really hard to get stains out of white towels. They were grey and another had bright red fingernail polish on it.

The pool was not finished; but, I suppose it will be, soon.

There is a security guard during the day; but, they really need one at night to keep the locals from roaming through the parking lot. One guy was collecting cans at 4:30 in the morning. I do not begrudge him his living, but I don't like having to watch my car at that time. (I wish the motel had a recycling bin, too.)

On the plus side, I do like the new recessed lighting; it's very nice and contemporary!

The front desk people were very nice, letting us check in early. Thank you!< /Text>< Pics>

<name>Lance Hotz< /name><Time>1521984651526<//Time>< Rate>
3< /Rate>
<review>This is going to be long and I apologize. If you only plan to spend two or three nights then this is a good place for you. If you are looking for a homey kind of room and planning for a longer stay you might need to look elsewhere. But please keep in mind this is a budget motel. Even with the negatives I would give this location three and a half stars.

My wife and I had to rent a motel room for several days while waiting for our new residence to be ready.
We chose Motel Six because it was pet friendly for our little dog. This Motel Six is not in the best area, with working girls around and doing what working girls do. However within the motel area we did feel secure. The room we stayed in was a very large corner room, over 200 square feet. The rooms have been recently remodeled and now they don't exactly shout "Welcome." Hospital sterile is not a good look, seriously.

The only things that break up the monotonous  walls are the window, an air conditioner, and a nice sized flat screen TV. There were no wall mounted lamps next to the large king size bed, not even the mandatory tacky artwork on the walls. The ceiling lighting is in keeping with the room design, recessed, white, and sterile, as if the designers didn't know they make flourescent light bulbs that duplicate the warm welcome feeling of the incandescent ones. In fact I even brought one of my own lamps from home.

The clothes hanging rack is miniscule, just two small posts protruding from the wall with not enough room between them to allow the hangers not to overlap each other. If you have more than eight items of clothing to hang I am afraid you are out of luck. Below that are three small shelves, the only places in this very large room to put folding clothes. Both of these will be an issue for any guy who has a wife or a girlfriend.

This leads to the lack of surfaces. There is a half table mounted to the wall along with two Spartan Ikea type chairs. The bathroom sink area didn't need to have such a small surface area, as to one side there was a fifteen inch empty space between it and the adjacent wall. Again remember the wives and girlfriends. There is no dresser or chest of drawers as is found in most motel rooms to store your clothes, thus there is no top surface on which to set anything either. In summary it is as if Motel 6 did the remodel on the cheap with no thought toward the convenience and comfort of its customers, especially leaving out wives and girlfriends.

That is too bad, since the staff there is great. I had no problems with the rudeness of the housekeeping staff of which other reviewers have mentioned. And if I did I wouldn't hold it against them. They are working at a hard minimum wage job, often with no tips for their good service. And the office staff are all very nice people, always willing to help with a friendly smile and that is a huge plus for travelers. I just wish that in this case at least Motel Six was on par with its employees.
PS: On the plus side Motel Six provides in room mini refrigerators. üòÅüòÅüòÅ< /review><Pics>None<//Pics>< resp>
None<//resp>
